# How To Generate Leads With Cold Email in 2026 (FULL COURSE)
*Expert:* Matt Lucero
*YouTube:* https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=BakY-82NYVQ
*Published:* 2026-04-12

## Key Takeaways
- Lead generation starts with a clear offer, a defined audience, and a reason the buyer should care.
- Cold email campaigns need list building, infrastructure, copy, and follow-up working together.
- A full-course format helps evaluate the whole pipeline rather than isolated email tips.
- The system should be measured from prospect selection through booked conversations.

---

[23:44] deliverability matters. Because the

[23:50] can't I just send you know a couple of
[23:52] emails? The reason why is because cold
[23:53] email and sales for that matter is
[23:55] fundamentally a numbers game. I say that
[23:58] because most people think they are
[23:59] selling a product or service they can go
[24:01] to five people and one of them is going
[24:03] to buy. But in reality, only 3% of a
[24:05] market at any given point is actively
[24:08] looking to buy the service that you
[24:09] have. So the more emails that you send,
[24:11] the more people that you're going to
[24:12] find. Most people that you're reaching
[24:13] out to, even if they're highly targeted
[24:15] or relevant people, aren't going to be
[24:17] in market for your service. So if you
[24:18] want to generate serious results and
[24:20] meetings for your business, volume is
[24:22] critical. Now, again, if you really just
[24:24] want a couple extra meetings per month
[24:25] and you're using cold email to get that
[24:27] done, you might not need to send a ton
[24:29] of emails. You might need to send a
[24:30] couple thousand a month. But if you're
[24:31] looking to generate 10 meetings a month,
[24:33] 20 meetings a month, 100 meetings a
[24:35] month, you're going to have to get in
[24:36] front of a lot of people because again,
[24:37] you have to think most of the people
[24:39] you're reaching out to aren't going to
[24:40] be interested in your service and are
[24:42] not going to be in market for your
[24:43] service, let alone trust you or think
[24:45] you're the right person. And so, you
[24:46] have to reach out to so many people just
[24:48] to get some of those people interested
[24:50] and a fraction of those people on a call
[24:51] and a fraction of those people to
[24:53] purchase your services or your product.
[24:55] So, just keep in mind that it is a
[24:56] numbers game. If you want to be able to

[25:00] that don't land in spam, you're going to

[02:39:04] similar. So, first we're going to cover
[02:39:05] the principles of writing good cold
[02:39:07] email copy. So, the first tip that I'm
[02:39:10] going to give to anybody who wants to
[02:39:11] send out cold emails, regardless of what
[02:39:14] you're doing, you need to have a good
[02:39:16] offer. Okay? The analogy I like to use
[02:39:18] is that you can only put so much
[02:39:19] lipstick on a pig. Because regardless of
[02:39:22] how good your copy is, if you have a
[02:39:24] terrible offer, no one is going to reply
[02:39:26] to your cold emails. And I mean, nobody.
[02:39:28] You can learn this the hard way by doing
[02:39:30] this yourself. I would not recommend it.
[02:39:33] Just try and start off by selling
[02:39:34] something that people want because I
[02:39:36] don't know about you, but this pig does
[02:39:38] not look very attractive to me. The
[02:39:40] lipstick only does so much. So, you can
[02:39:42] only do so much with your copy to make
[02:39:44] your offer sound good. But if you just
[02:39:46] have a terrible offer, then nobody's
[02:39:47] going to want to respond to your cold
[02:39:49] emails. You're not going to get any
[02:39:50] meetings booked and it's just going to
[02:39:51] be a disaster. So, how to make your
[02:39:53] offer better? The number one thing you
[02:39:54] can do is lower risk for the people
[02:39:56] buying your stuff. You can do this in
[02:39:58] two ways. By either guaranteeing results
[02:40:00] or working on a performance basis.
[02:40:02] Personally, in my agency, I work on a
[02:40:04] performance basis. Other people
[02:40:05] guarantee results, and you can do both.
[02:40:07] What this basically does is it makes it
[02:40:09] more of a no-brainer for someone who
[02:40:11] wants to buy your service. Because if
[02:40:13] you guarantee results or you work on
[02:40:14] performance, then the chances of them
[02:40:16] getting the actual result that you're
[02:40:18] guaranteeing is a million times higher.
[02:40:20] The second point that I would say to
[02:40:21] make your offer better is to solve
[02:40:23] actual pain points in the market. I say
[02:40:25] this because some people just try and
[02:40:27] sell stuff that the market doesn't want.
[02:40:29] A perfect example is saturation. And a
[02:40:31] lot of people think that market
[02:40:32] saturation is a bad thing when in
[02:40:34] reality it's a good thing because it
